       ) which was mostly written during the Japanese occupation was published by the Instituto June 28, 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       King
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">
        Juan Carlos I
       </a>
       commented in 2007 that, "In fact, some of the beautiful pages of Spanish literature were written in the Philippines".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During her visit to the Philippines in July 2012,
       <a href="/wiki/Queen_Sof%C3%ADa_of_Spain" title="Queen Sofía of Spain">
        Sofia of Spain
       </a>
       expressed her support for the Spanish language to be revived in Philippine schools.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 11, 2012, saying that there were 318 Spanish-trained basic education teachers in the Philippines, Philippine secretary of the Department of Education
       <a href="/wiki/Armin_Luistro" title="Armin Luistro">
        Armin Luistro
       </a>
       announced an agreement with the
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chilean
       </a>
       government to train Filipino school teachers in Spanish. In exchange, the Philippines would help train Chilean teachers in English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_status">
        Current status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Current status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Since the independence of the Philippines from Spain (1898), the dialect has lost most of its speakers and it might be now close to disappearing.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Spanish was the language of government, education and trade throughout the three centuries (333 years) of the Philippines being part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       and continued to serve as a
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       until the first half of the 20th century. In the last decades its use has declined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New developments in the Philippines are slowly reversing this trend.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2007, former
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Philippines" title="President of the Philippines">
        President
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" title="Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">
        Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo
       </a>
       signed a directive in
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       that require the teaching and learning of the Spanish language in the Philippine school system starting in 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The presidential decision had immediate results. The Under-Secretary of the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Education_(Philippines)" title="Department of Education (Philippines)">
        Department of Education
       </a>
       , Vilma L. Labrador, circulated a Memorandum (17/XII/2007), on the
       <i>
        "Restoration of the Spanish language in Philippine Education"
       </i>
       . In it, the Department mandates secondary schools to offer basic and advanced Spanish.
      </p>
      <p>
       There has been a resurgence of learning Spanish among Filipinos, for various reasons. Interest in the language and recuperation of it as part of their history, namely their written, cultural history, interest in their connection to the Spanish-speaking world, among others.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to the huge demand for Spanish speakers among
       <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" title="Business process outsourcing">
        business process outsourcing
       </a>
       companies in the Philippines, Filipinos are flocking to
       <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">
        Instituto Cervantes
       </a>
       and other language centers in order to learn Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="clarify-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">
        For most of the less educated population, Spanish is acquired through
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_music" title="Hispanic music">
         Hispanic music
        </a>
        , or for some, especially children, by watching
        <a href="/wiki/Dora_the_Explorer" title="Dora the Explorer">
         Dora the Explorer
        </a>
        in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_(TV_channel)" title="Nickelodeon (TV channel)">
         Nickelodeon
        </a>
        . For the educated population, Spanish is further enriched through watching
        <a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">
         Telenovelas
        </a>
        from the internet or watching the cable channel of
        <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Televisión Española">
         Televisión Española
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
         <a href="#cite_note-79">
          [79]
         </a>
        </sup>
        That results in the lack of general characteristics that describe its phonological system.
       </span>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Clarify" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="Does this deal with native or 2nd language speakers? (October 2016)">
           clarify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2012
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , of the younger generation of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">
        Filipino Hispanophones
       </a>
       are following the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">
        Spanish orthographic
       </a>
       convention of typing letters with
       <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">
        diacritic marks
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
        acute accents
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">
        diaeresis
       </a>
       ) as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/Inverted_question_and_exclamation_marks" title="Inverted question and exclamation marks">
        inverted question and exclamation marks
       </a>
       and the rest of the special characters and symbols found in
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">
        Spanish orthography
       </a>
       on their US standard layout computer keyboards by using the
       <a href="/wiki/AltGr_key" title="AltGr key">
        AltGr key
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Modifier_key" title="Modifier key">
        Modifier key
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Code_page_437" title="Code page 437">
        Code page 437
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Code_page_850" title="Code page 850">
        Code page 850
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">
        Microsoft Windows
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alt_Key" title="Alt Key">
        Alt Key
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Alt_code" title="Alt code">
        Numeric Codes
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Character_(symbol)" title="Character (symbol)">
        character
       </a>
       shortcuts, or the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US-International" title="US-International">
        US-International
       </a>
       keyboard layout.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Spanish-language media is still present in the Philippines, the country has one Spanish newspaper,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/E-Dyario" title="E-Dyario">
         E-Dyario
        </a>
       </i>
       , the first Spanish digital newspaper published in the Philippines,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="Does this still exist? (September 2017)">
           needs update?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Filipinas,_Ahora_Mismo" title="Filipinas, Ahora Mismo">
         Filipinas, Ahora Mismo
        </a>
       </i>
       was a nationally syndicated, 60-minute, cultural radio magazine program in the Philippines broadcast daily in Spanish for two years in the 2000s.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_the_languages_of_the_Philippines">
        Influence on the languages of the Philippines
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Influence on the languages of the Philippines">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_language" title="Old Spanish language">
        Old Spanish language
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linguistic_history_of_Spanish" title="Linguistic history of Spanish">
        Linguistic history of Spanish
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are approximately 4,000 Spanish words in Tagalog (between 20% and 33% of Tagalog words),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newprospects_61-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-newprospects-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and around 6,000 Spanish words in Visayan and other Philippine languages. The Spanish counting system, calendar, time, etc. are still in use with slight modifications. Archaic Spanish words have been preserved in Tagalog and the other vernaculars, such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pera#Spanish" title="wikt:pera">
          pera
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        coins
       </i>
       ),
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sab%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:sabón">
          sabón
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       [
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/jab%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:jabón">
          jabón
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) at the beginning of Spanish rule, the
       <i>
        j
       </i>
       used to be pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
        voiceless postalveolar fricative
       </a>
       or the "sh" sound; (
       <i>
        soap
       </i>
       )],
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/relos#Spanish" title="wikt:relos">
          relos
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       [(
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/reloj#Spanish" title="wikt:reloj">
          reloj
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) with the
       <i>
        j
       </i>
       sound; (
       <i>
        watch
       </i>
       )],
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/kwarta#Spanish" title="wikt:kwarta">
          kwarta
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuarta#Spanish" title="wikt:cuarta">
          cuarta
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <i>
        money
       </i>
       ), etc.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Spaniards and the language are referred to as either
       <i>
        Kastila
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Katsila
       </i>
       (mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Visayan_languages" title="Visayan languages">
        Visayan languages
       </a>
       ) after
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Castilla#Spanish" title="wikt:Castilla">
          Castilla
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">
         Castile
        </a>
       </i>
       ), the original Spanish Kingdom under which Spain was unified in 1492, which later became a Spanish region.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Chavacano" title="Chavacano">
        Chavacano
       </a>
       (also called Zamboangueño), is a Spanish-based creole language spoken mainly in the southern province of Zamboanga and, to a much lesser extent, in the province of Cavite in the northern region of
       <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">
        Luzon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chavacano became the main language in the
       <a href="/wiki/Zamboanga_City" title="Zamboanga City">
        Zamboanga City
       </a>
       and some parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Zamboanga_Peninsula" title="Zamboanga Peninsula">
        Zamboanga Peninsula
       </a>
       , as a result of the migration into the area of a large number of workers, who came from different linguistic regions to build military and other Spanish establishments.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphosemantic_changes">
        Morphosemantic changes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Morphosemantic changes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_dialects_and_varieties" title="Spanish dialects and varieties">
        Spanish dialects and varieties
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       While many Spanish words have entered Tagalog, Cebuano, Waray-Waray, and other Philippine languages, many of the words have seen a shift in meaning and even construction from the original Spanish. That has resulted in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/False_friends" title="False friends">
        false friends
       </a>
       , similar words in both languages but with a different meaning. A sample is shown below:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Word
        </th>
        <th>
         Language
        </th>
        <th>
         Meaning in the Philippines
        </th>
        <th>
         Original Spanish word
        </th>
        <th>
         Spanish meaning
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         asár
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Ilocano, Kapampangan, Chavacano (spelled as asá meaning roast or to roast)
        </td>
        <td>
         to annoy
        </td>
        <td>
         asar
        </td>
        <td>
         roast
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         astá
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Kapampangan, Hiligaynon (until), Chavacano (hasta meaning until or til then)
        </td>
        <td>
         rude movements
        </td>
        <td>
         hasta (in Arabic: Hatta) Influences from Latin ad ista (“to this”)
        </td>
        <td>
         until
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         bale
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Kapampangan, Hiligaynon, Chavacano (spelled as Vale for nice, beautiful)
        </td>
        <td>
         well and worth, ie/'that is to say'/namely, wages, advance pay
        </td>
        <td>
         vale
        </td>
        <td>
         ok! and voucher or promissory note
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         balón
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Kapampangan, Visayan, Chavacano
        </td>
        <td>
         well/balloon
        </td>
        <td>
         balón
        </td>
        <td>
         ball
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         banda
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Kapampangan, Hiligaynon, Chavacano
        </td>
        <td>
         within proximity of and band
        </td>
        <td>
         banda
        </td>
        <td>
         band, side
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         baráto
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Ilocano, Hiligaynon, Kapampangan
        </td>
        <td>
         cheap
        </td>
        <td>
         barato
        </td>
        <td>
         cheap, low prices
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         barkada
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Cebuano, Ilocano, Pangasinense, Kapampangan, Hiligaynon
        </td>
        <td>
         group of friends
        </td>
        <td>
         barcada
        </td>
        <td>
         boatload
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         basta
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Chavacano (also retains original meaning), Cebuano, Hiligaynon, Kapampangan
        </td>
        <td>
         as long as/secret
        </td>
        <td>
         basta
        </td>
        <td>
         enough, stop!
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         bida
        </td>
        <td>
         Tagalog, Cebuano, Ilocano, Kapampangan, Chavacano (spelled as Vida)
        </td>
        <td>
         lead actor or actress
        </td>
        <td>
         vida
        </td>
        <td>
         life
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         bomba
        </td>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="False_cognates">
        False cognates
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: False cognates">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following words do not fall under false friends. They are still a source of confusion:
      </p>

         Spanish meaning
        </th>
       </tr>

        </td>

         village judge who decided on irrigation distribution or official who measured weights
        </td>
       </tr>

         <br/>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Spanish_words_of_Philippine_origin">
        List of Spanish words of Philippine origin
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: List of Spanish words of Philippine origin">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Influences_on_the_Spanish_language" title="Influences on the Spanish language">
        Influences on the Spanish language
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          <img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
         <b>
          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
           IPA
          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Although the greatest linguistic impact and
       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">
        loanwords
       </a>
       have been from Spanish to the languages of the Philippines, the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_languages" title="Philippine languages">
        Philippine languages
       </a>
       have also loaned some words to Spanish.
      </p>
      <p>
       The following are some of the words of Philippine origin that can be found in the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diccionario_de_la_lengua_espa%C3%B1ola_de_la_Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Diccionario de la lengua española de la Real Academia Española">
         Diccionario de la lengua española de la Real Academia Española
        </a>
       </i>
       , the dictionary published by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        Real Academia Española
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable">
       <tr>

        </th>
        <th>
         Via
        </th>
        <th>
         Tagalog
        </th>
        <th>
         English equivalent
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>

          abacá
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">
          Old Tagalog
         </a>
         : abacá
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         abaká
        </td>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abaca" title="Abaca">
          abaca
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a class="external text" href="http://buscon.rae.es/draeI/SrvltConsulta?TIPO_BUS=3&amp;LEMA=baguio" rel="nofollow">
          baguio
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
       <ol class="references">
        <li id="cite_note-official_languages-1">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-official_languages_1-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-official_languages_1-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-official_languages_1-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Article XIV, Section 3 of the
          <a class="external text" href="http://thecorpusjuris.com/laws/constitutions/item/1935-constitution.html" rel="nofollow">
           1935 Philippine Constitution
          </a>
          provided, "[...] Until otherwise provided by law, English and Spanish shall continue as official languages." The
          <a class="external text" href="http://thecorpusjuris.com/laws/constitutions/item/1943-constitution.html" rel="nofollow">
           1943 Philippine Constitution
          </a>
          (in effect during occupation by Japanese forces, and later repudiated) did not specify official languages. Article XV, Section 3(3) of the
          <a class="external text" href="http://thecorpusjuris.com/laws/constitutions/item/1973-constitution.html" rel="nofollow">
           1973 Philippine constitution
          </a>
          ratified on January 17, 1973 specified, "Until otherwise provided by law, English and Pilipino shall be the official languages.
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.chanrobles.com/presidentialdecrees/presidentialdecreeno155.html" rel="nofollow">
           Presidential Decree No. 155
          </a>
          dated March 15, 1973 ordered, "[...] that the Spanish language shall continue to be recognized as an official language in the Philippines while important documents in government files are in the Spanish language and not translated into either English or Pilipino language." Article XIV Section 7 of the
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.gov.ph/constitutions/the-1987-constitution-of-the-republic-of-the-philippines/the-1987-constitution-of-the-republic-of-the-philippines-article-xiv/" rel="nofollow">
           1987 Philippine Constitution
          </a>
          specified, "For purposes of communication and instruction, the official languages of the Philippines are Filipino and, until otherwise provided by law, English."
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-voluntary_and_optional-2">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-voluntary_and_optional_2-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-voluntary_and_optional_2-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <b>
           Article XIV, Sec 7
          </b>
          : For purposes of communication and instruction, the official languages of the Philippines are Filipino and, until otherwise provided by law, English. The regional languages are the auxiliary official languages in the regions and shall serve as auxiliary media of instruction therein.
          <b>
           Spanish
          </b>
          and Arabic shall be promoted on a voluntary and optional basis.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-florentino-3">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-florentino_3-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-florentino_3-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-florentino_3-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-florentino_3-3">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              d
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation journal" id="CITEREFRodao1997">
           Rodao, Florentino (1997).
           <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/query?url=http%3A%2F%2Fcat.inist.fr%2F%3FaModele%3DafficheN%26cpsidt%3D2877788&amp;date=2010-07-13" rel="nofollow">
            "Spanish language in the Philippines : 1900–1940"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            Philippine studies
           </i>
           . 12. Manila, Philippines: Ateneo de Manila University Press.
           <b>
            45
           </b>
           (1): 94–107.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">
            ISSN
           </a>
           <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0031-7837" rel="nofollow">
            0031-7837
           </a>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">
            OCLC
           </a>
           <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/612174151" rel="nofollow">
            612174151
           </a>
           . Archived from
           <a class="external text" href="http://cat.inist.fr/?aModele=afficheN&amp;cpsidt=2877788" rel="nofollow">
            the original
           </a>
           on July 13, 2010
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             July 14,
            </span>
            2010
           </span>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Philippine+studies&amp;rft.atitle=Spanish+language+in+the+Philippines+%3A+1900%E2%80%931940&amp;rft.volume=45&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=94-107&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F612174151&amp;rft.issn=0031-7837&amp;rft.aulast=Rodao&amp;rft.aufirst=Florentino&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcat.inist.fr%2F%3FaModele%3DafficheN%26cpsidt%3D2877788&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+language+in+the+Philippines">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-1897and1899-4">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-1897and1899_4-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-1897and1899_4-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-1897and1899_4-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The
          <a href="/wiki/Malolos_Constitution" title="Malolos Constitution">
           Malolos Constitution
          </a>
          was written in Spanish, and no official English translation was released. Article 93 read, "Artículo 93.° El empleo de las lenguas usadas en Filipinas es potestativo. No puede regularse sino por la ley y solamente para los actos de la autoridad pública y los asuntos judiciales. Para estos actos se usará por ahora la lengua castellana.";
          <br/>
          A literal translation originally printed as exhibit IV, Volume I,
          <i>
           Report of the Philippine Commission to the President
          </i>
          , January 31, 1900, Senate Document 188. Fifty-sixth Congress, first session.) read, "ART.93 The use of the languages spoken in the Philippines is optional. It can only be regulated by law, and solely as regards acts of public authority and judicial affairs. For these acts, the Spanish language shall be used for the time being.",
          <a href="#CITEREFKalaw1927">
           Kalaw 1927
          </a>
          , p.
          <a class="external text" href="http://quod.lib.umich.edu/cgi/t/text/pageviewer-idx?c=philamer;cc=philamer;idno=afj2233.0001.001;frm=frameset;view=image;seq=463;page=root;size=s" rel="nofollow">
           443
          </a>
          ;
          <br/>
          In 1972, the Philippine Government
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Historical_Institute" title="National Historical Institute">
           National Historical Institute
          </a>
          (NHI) published
          <a href="#CITEREFGuevara1972">
           Guevara 1972
          </a>
          , which contained a somewhat different English translation in which Article 93 read, "Article 93. The use of languages spoken in the Philippines shall be optional. Their use cannot be regulated except by virtue of law, and solely for acts of public authority and in the courts. For these acts the Spanish language may be used in the meantime."
          <a href="#CITEREFGuevara1972">
           Guevara 1972
          </a>
          , p.
          <a class="external text" href="http://quod.lib.umich.edu/cgi/t/text/pageviewer-idx?c=philamer;cc=philamer;idno=aab1246.0001.001;frm=frameset;view=image;seq=135;page=root;size=s" rel="nofollow">
           117
          </a>
          ;
          <br/>
          Other translations also exist (e.g.
          <a href="#CITEREFRodriguez1997">
           Rodriguez 1997
          </a>
          , p.
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=l8alSTTrk48C&amp;pg=PA130" rel="nofollow">
           130
          </a>
          );
          <br/>
          As of 2008, the NHI translation seems to predominate in publication, with some sources describing it as "official" or "approved":
          <a href="#CITEREFRappaWee2006">
           Rappa &amp; Wee 2006
          </a>
          , p.
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=KXQTIl2eox4C&amp;pg=PA67" rel="nofollow">
           67
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="#CITEREFWoods2005">
           Woods 2005
          </a>
          , p.
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=2Z-n_kDTxf0C&amp;pg=PA218" rel="nofollow">
           218
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="#CITEREFCorpus_Juris">
           Corpus Juris
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="#CITEREFLawPhil">
           LawPhil
          </a>
          ; (others).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-zamboanga-5">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-zamboanga_5-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-zamboanga_5-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/5rfy8a79R?url=http://www.zamboanga.com/history/republic_of_zamboanga.html" rel="nofollow">
            "History of The Republic of Zamboanga (May 1899 – March 1903)"

             <li>
              <i>
               Italics
              </i>
              indicate
              <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
               extinct languages
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <b>
               Bold
              </b>
              indicates
              <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
               languages with more than 5 million speakers
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              Languages between parentheses are
              <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
               varieties
              </a>
              of the language on their left.
